<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17082116616957037181">Miles Ryan's life seemed to end the day his wife was killed in a hit-and-run accident two years ago. Missy had been his first love, and Miles fervently believes she will be his last. As a deputy in the North Carolina town of New Bern, Miles Ryan not only grieves for Missy, but also longs to bring the unknown driver to justice. Then Miles meets Sarah Andrews. The second gra</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17082116616957037181">Miles Ryan's life seemed to end the day his wife was killed in a hit-and-run accident two years ago. Missy had been his first love, and Miles fervently believes she will be his last. As a deputy in the North Carolina town of New Bern, Miles Ryan not only grieves for Missy, but also longs to bring the unknown driver to justice. Then Miles meets Sarah Andrews. The second grade teacher of his son, Jonah, Sarah had left Baltimore after a difficult divorce to start over in the gentler surroundings of New Bern. Perhaps it's her own emotional wounds that make her sensitive to the hurt she first sees in Jonah's eyes, and then his father's.<br /><br />Tentatively, Sarah and Miles reach out to each other. Soon they are both laughing for the first time in years . . . and falling in love. Neither will be able to guess how closely linked they are to a shocking secret -- one that will force them to question everything they ever believed in . . . and make a heartbreaking choice that will change their lives forever.<br /><br />In A Bend in the Road, Nicholas Sparks writes with a luminous intensity about life's bitter turns and incomparable sweetness. His affirming message carries a powerful lesson about the imperfections of being human, the mistakes we all make, and the joy that comes when we give ourselves to love.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17082116616957037181">...more</a>

<div class="questionText">
<a href="/questions/117045-could-it-have-a-better-climax">could it have a better climax ?</a>
</div>
<div class="communityQAFooter questionFooter">
<ul class="questionFooterActions">
<li class="footerItem like">
<span id="like_container_community_question_117045" class="likeItContainer"><a href="http://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F969943.A_Bend_in_the_Road" class="jsLike like_it" rel="nofollow">like</a></span>

</li>

<a href="/questions/117045-could-it-have-a-better-climax">See all 3 answers</a>

<div class="allCommunityAnswers">
<div class="communityAnswer">
<div class="communityAnswerBody">
<div class="answererUserIcon">
<a href="/user/show/8408770-lisa-lathrop" class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto"><img src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/users/1418953964i/8408770._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" alt="" /></a>
</div>
<div class="communityAnswerTextContainer">
<span class="communityAnswererName">
<a href="/user/show/8408770-lisa-lathrop">Lisa Lathrop</a>
</span>
<span class="communityAnswerText">
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Sure...Miles could have really gotten out of hand with his anger. It really got annoying..and especially his desire to kill almost anyone/anything. It<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Sure...Miles could have really gotten out of hand with his anger. It really got annoying..and especially his desire to kill almost anyone/anything. It got old. That being said, I suspect many people would act the same after having their wife and son's mother taken away too soon. I would have rather seen Miles take more than a few days break from Sarah....it would have been interesting to see it play out how he enjoyed Jonah's company again on their getaway. People need space to think and process these things. In my mind, Sparks could have added a chapter at least to allow us to see the healing process of Miles. <a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

  <a href="/user/show/66513-m-m-sana" class="left imgcol" title="M. M. Sana"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1252978526p2/66513.jpg" alt="M. M. Sana" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/908397?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 26, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/66513-m-m-sana" class="user" title="M. M. Sana">M. M. Sana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/3463.A_Bend_in_the_Road" title="Paperback 9780446696135" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Light Mystery/Drama Readers</span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer908397">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6182539705941286678">This is an awesome book. It has a little bit of romance and a little mystery. It will embed images in your mind that will be hard to escape. Love and forgiveness will have a new meaning in your life. Yes, it does have a little bit of everything. A husband's love, a father's love, a cop in action, romance, mystery... FORGIVENESS! I won't tell you what it is about, because I think you should read it. REALLY!!! Go get it and read it. I never thought a man could write LOVE so well. Love in its pures</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6182539705941286678">This is an awesome book. It has a little bit of romance and a little mystery. It will embed images in your mind that will be hard to escape. Love and forgiveness will have a new meaning in your life. Yes, it does have a little bit of everything. A husband's love, a father's love, a cop in action, romance, mystery... FORGIVENESS! I won't tell you what it is about, because I think you should read it. REALLY!!! Go get it and read it. I never thought a man could write LOVE so well. Love in its purest form.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_140884908">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140884908" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3099666-buggy" class="left imgcol" title="Buggy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1289702969p2/3099666.jpg" alt="Buggy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/140884908?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 18, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3099666-buggy" class="user" title="Buggy">Buggy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/3463.A_Bend_in_the_Road" title="Paperback 9780446696135" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=contemp-rom" class="actionLinkLite">contemp-rom</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=tortured-hero" class="actionLinkLite">tortured-hero</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=men-in-uniform-pc-ff" class="actionLinkLite">men-in-uniform-pc-ff</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=shelf-11" class="actionLinkLite">shelf-11</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer140884908">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5110482864819809389">Opening Line:<em> “On the morning of August 29, 1988, a little more than two years after his wife had passed away, Miles Ryan stood on the back porch of his house, smoking a cigarette, watching as the rising sun slowly changed the morning sky from dusky grey to orange.”</em><br /><br />Nicholas Sparks is like comfort food, I always know going in the kind of emotional love story I’m going to get and I can count on being sucked into the lives, loves and heartache of his small town characters. They’re written realistic</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5110482864819809389">Opening Line:<em> “On the morning of August 29, 1988, a little more than two years after his wife had passed away, Miles Ryan stood on the back porch of his house, smoking a cigarette, watching as the rising sun slowly changed the morning sky from dusky grey to orange.”</em><br /><br />Nicholas Sparks is like comfort food, I always know going in the kind of emotional love story I’m going to get and I can count on being sucked into the lives, loves and heartache of his small town characters. They’re written realistically, I mean I feel like I know them, flaws and all and I usually want to move to whatever town it is he’s describing. Sure sometimes the stories are predictable and I find that the couple de jour spouts the “I love you’s” too soon for my liking or realism’s sake but still his stories are always a pleasure to read, which is what keeps me coming back for more.<br /><br />A BEND IN THE ROAD was a surprise in that it keeps a sense of mystery going throughout, often leaving the main couples love story and allowing us into the mind of the anonymous “bad guy”. Slowly unravelling their story until the shocking big reveal at the end. I honestly didn’t know how Sparks was going to wrap things up here, his couples doesn’t always end up together and that too added to the mystery.<br /><br />Sheriff’s deputy Miles Ryan is still struggling to come to terms with the death of his beloved wife in a hit-and-run accident nearly two years ago. High school sweethearts, theirs was a love destined to last and Miles can’t seem to let go of the grief or the fact that as an officer of the law he’s been unable to find the person responsible. If it weren’t for their young son Jonah it’s unlikely that Miles would find the strength to get through the day. <br /><br />Which brings into play Jonah’s second grade teacher Sarah Andrews. When Jonah begins having trouble keeping up in school Sarah offers to tutor him and a tentative relationship begins to form. Sarah is running away from a bad divorce (is there a good one?) and has a few skeletons in her closet as well. Our couple fall in love pretty fast (from one page to the next) and are just beginning to see a real future together when Miles’ past comes back, tearing everything apart. Unwilling to let go of his dead wife and obsessed with finding her killer and ultimately closure I can honestly say that I was surprised by events I didn’t see coming. <br /><br />As I hinted at earlier I really enjoyed getting inside the head of the hit-and-run driver and slowly discovering who it was, becoming very sympathetic towards their situation. However I could have done without spending so much time running around with county sheriff Charlie and subsequently the middle parts of this story lagged. Still a recommended read. Cheers!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5110482864819809389">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Nicholas Spark fans</span></div>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Alaine by: </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1051989-alaine?shelf=general-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">general-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer35036615">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14687462598978636587">Some stories don't have happy endings and some do. This one of course can't really have a happy ending because a wife and mother have died. But, this book tells the story of a man's journey through grief, and anyone who has been through the loss of a loved one knows that the pain never ends. Nicholas Sparks did a wonderful job of reminding us of that, it was not a week love story, someone dies, someone else comes along and they live happily ever after. Instead it spoke clearly of the struggle an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14687462598978636587">Some stories don't have happy endings and some do. This one of course can't really have a happy ending because a wife and mother have died. But, this book tells the story of a man's journey through grief, and anyone who has been through the loss of a loved one knows that the pain never ends. Nicholas Sparks did a wonderful job of reminding us of that, it was not a week love story, someone dies, someone else comes along and they live happily ever after. Instead it spoke clearly of the struggle and inner turmoil of a man wanting to get on with his life but never really being able to let go. He had the flashbacks and constant memories that we all have when going through grief. This aspect of the book was excellent and could not be faulted.<br />Whilst I loved the character of Sarah I struggled to make that emotional connection to Miles. For me I found him to be a little bit of a typical macho kind of guy and that at times annoyed me. I will say however that it is possible that I had this issue because I listened to this book on audio and sometimes the droning of characters can get on your nerves. This is however the reason I gave the book a rating of 3 (although, it would be 3 1/2 if it where possible) and not higher, I just didn't fall in love with the main character the way that I wanted to.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer87100493">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7533960713592050156">This novel was like reading the Cliff Notes of a epic love story, MINUS the analysis and depth you might find in Cliff Notes and MINUS the well-developed and fascinating characters, settings and dialogue you might find in an epic love story. Based upon my reading of this book, nobody will be reading Nicolas Sparks 100 years from now and I refuse to waste any more of my limited time on Earth reading words slapped together by him and bound under the pretense of actually being a novel.<br /><br />The SECOND BE</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7533960713592050156">This novel was like reading the Cliff Notes of a epic love story, MINUS the analysis and depth you might find in Cliff Notes and MINUS the well-developed and fascinating characters, settings and dialogue you might find in an epic love story. Based upon my reading of this book, nobody will be reading Nicolas Sparks 100 years from now and I refuse to waste any more of my limited time on Earth reading words slapped together by him and bound under the pretense of actually being a novel.<br /><br />The SECOND BEST thing about A Bend in the Road is that it was only 368 pages (with medium-large type) and it was over quickly. In spite of this, I'm still surprised I finished it. The few times I did put it down, I threw it down disgusted by his formulaic writing style, predictable plot lines and pathetic dialogue.<br /><br />The BEST thing about A Bend in the Road is that one month - maybe even one week - from now, I won't be able to remember a damn thing about it. No aspect of this book is memorable and essentially every aspect of it is utterly forgettable.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1033576387">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2845784967209402701">What does a man do when the love of his life is killed by a hit and run driver while jogging? And this love of his life is not only his childhood sweetheart, but also his wife and mother of his son, Jonah. Sheriff Miles Ryan felt he died the night his wife Missy was fatally struck, but was determined to find her killer and spent the next two years focused on investigating every lead.<br /><br />While Miles immersed himself with his search, seven-year-old Jonah suffered. He missed not only his mother, but al</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2845784967209402701">What does a man do when the love of his life is killed by a hit and run driver while jogging? And this love of his life is not only his childhood sweetheart, but also his wife and mother of his son, Jonah. Sheriff Miles Ryan felt he died the night his wife Missy was fatally struck, but was determined to find her killer and spent the next two years focused on investigating every lead.<br /><br />While Miles immersed himself with his search, seven-year-old Jonah suffered. He missed not only his mother, but also his father's attention, causing his school work to suffer. Sarah Andrews, Jonah's teacher, decided to step in to set things right by suggesting Jonah needed tutoring and to her astonishment offered to help him after school, which she wouldn't normally do. She develops a fondness for Jonah and feels an attraction to the handsome sheriff, whom she starts dating. Before long she realizes she is falling in love with Miles, though she knows a relationship is unlikely for he is still in love with his dead wife. But Miles is surprised to find himself falling for Sarah and plans to spend the rest of his life with her.<br /><br />One night while on patrol, Miles arrests a local for drunk driving. Because this man is on parole, knowing he'll be sent back to jail, he tells Miles he knows who killed Missy, but won't impart that information unless Miles lets him off. Though it was wrong, but needing to know the truth about Missy's death, Miles goes against the rules to get this information. Only thing, the information is wrong and Miles goes after the wrong man--a man who has been a thorn in his side for years. While Miles is seeking vengeance, Sarah learns the truth and realizes she must tell him, but knows that by doing so would kill any chance for them. Sick at heart, she does the right thing, and Miles, feeling betrayed lashes out terminating their relationship.<br /><br />Mr. Sparks grabs the reader's emotions, enabling them to feel his characters' pain. This is a story that sticks long after the last page.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2845784967209402701">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer226998206">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7830685247701627236"> There are some authors that are "go-to" for me. When I am in need of a quick read, not mindless but neither exceedingly deep, I turn to Nicholas Sparks. I know when I pick up one of his books, I will leave satisfied.This one was no exception.<br /> Miles Ryan has been struggling over the past two years to find his footing in life after his wife Missy was killed in a hit and run. Just how disconnected he has been is brought home when he finds out how badly his son Jonah is doing in school.<br /> Determined</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7830685247701627236"> There are some authors that are "go-to" for me. When I am in need of a quick read, not mindless but neither exceedingly deep, I turn to Nicholas Sparks. I know when I pick up one of his books, I will leave satisfied.This one was no exception.<br /> Miles Ryan has been struggling over the past two years to find his footing in life after his wife Missy was killed in a hit and run. Just how disconnected he has been is brought home when he finds out how badly his son Jonah is doing in school.<br /> Determined to move forward and do right by his son,Miles is drawn to Jonah's teacher, Sarah. After some fits and starts, they draw closer and fall in love. But life's path is full of twists and turns and ugliness will rear it's head. But no matter how imperfect we are, our capacity to love and forgive is great.<br /> As much a mystery as a romance,I liked that the driver in the accident had a voice. It wasn't difficult to figure out who it was, and I was left to puzzle how the romance would fare when the perpetrator was finally revealed.<br /> And as always, I enjoy reading books centered in my adopted home state of North Carolina. So, I have had my fix and am ready to move on. Thanks, Nick.<br /></span>

  <a href="/user/show/2973969-gorfo" class="left imgcol" title="Gorfo"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1370016023p2/2973969.jpg" alt="Gorfo" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/102817551?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 30, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2973969-gorfo" class="user" title="Gorfo">Gorfo</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/3463.A_Bend_in_the_Road" title="Paperback 9780446696135" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Gorfo by: </span>
      cara
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2973969-gorfo?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2973969-gorfo?shelf=realistic" class="actionLinkLite">realistic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer102817551">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2884532458893602734"> A Bend in the Road is not the story to take with you on a road trip. The books tells the story of Mile's Ryan's life after the death of his wife Missy Ryan. Not surprisingly the story becomes a love story when Deputy Ryan meets and falls in love with his sons' second grade teacher Sarah. It turns out that Sarah is heartbroken too and the two hit it off after Miles sweeps her off her feet with his superb elegance (not). Nothing seems to threaten their relationship until (dun dun dun) new informa</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2884532458893602734"> A Bend in the Road is not the story to take with you on a road trip. The books tells the story of Mile's Ryan's life after the death of his wife Missy Ryan. Not surprisingly the story becomes a love story when Deputy Ryan meets and falls in love with his sons' second grade teacher Sarah. It turns out that Sarah is heartbroken too and the two hit it off after Miles sweeps her off her feet with his superb elegance (not). Nothing seems to threaten their relationship until (dun dun dun) new information about Missy's hit and run killer resurfaces.<br /><br />What really bothered me about this book was the utter predictability! Miles became a complete monster after he started to focus on the case once more and I half-thought that Sarah would end up breaking up with him because he threatened to be violent. Of course she stood by him because this is after a Nicholas Sparks novel filled to the brim with steadfast true love. The book had that "expect the unexpected" quality which didn't quite work out. Because of the lack of characters you can have the "killer" pegged almost right off the bat.<br /><br />It bothers me that so many of Nicholas Spark's books are set in this "small town" of New Bern. If it's such a small town do all the characters know each other? I just wish there would be a change of setting.<br /><br />Finally everything about this novel is soooo cliche! Looking at the dialogue I sometimes think "does anybody even talk like this?". <br /><br />There's no denying however that there is some good in this book. The plot twist in A Bend in the Road was excellent! I didn't even see it coming!<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2884532458893602734">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2500098-kereesa?shelf=books-i-ll-never-read-again" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-ll-never-read-again</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2500098-kereesa?shelf=2011" class="actionLinkLite">2011</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2500098-kereesa?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2500098-kereesa?shelf=hype-fail" class="actionLinkLite">hype-fail</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer191600452">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer620266305225313112">A Bend in the Road is about the intersecting lives of Miles Ryan, one of the town's deputies who's lost his wife in a hit and run accident about two years and is now raising his only son Jonah, and Jonah's teacher and recently divorcee Sarah Andrews. Obviously they fall in love, and obstacles, this would be where the 'bend' in the road occurs, fall in their way in this tale of forgiveness and romance.<br /><br />*gag*<br /><br />Right, so I was recommended this book by my co-worker who I made read the Hunger Games, and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText620266305225313112">A Bend in the Road is about the intersecting lives of Miles Ryan, one of the town's deputies who's lost his wife in a hit and run accident about two years and is now raising his only son Jonah, and Jonah's teacher and recently divorcee Sarah Andrews. Obviously they fall in love, and obstacles, this would be where the 'bend' in the road occurs, fall in their way in this tale of forgiveness and romance.<br /><br />*gag*<br /><br />Right, so I was recommended this book by my co-worker who I made read the Hunger Games, and wanted to see what I'd think of a book she really liked. <br /><br />Well.<br /><br />So the book isn't absolutely terrible. The romance is overthetop cheesy, the writing makes me die, and I just didn't care throughout the whole thing. But there were moments where I was entranced, and I liked the book to some degree. I won't be reading anything else by Sparks, probably, but hey it was fun.<br /><br />For entertainment purposes only, here are two things that I noticed were a bit abundant throughout the novel:<br /><br />A. Everyone smells everyone's hair. Especially Jonah's. SURPRISINGLY they all smell like SHAMPOO. Who'd thunk it? Also, that's kind of weird, shampoo shouldn't be that strong, I think anyway. <br /><br />B. EVERY. SINGLE. PERSON. IN. THIS. DAMN. BOOK. RUNS. THEIR. FINGERS. THROUGH. THEIR. HAIR. Seriously! Miles is the worst at it, I can't count the number of times he 'runs his fingers through his hair' and it fluffed up or something like that. I started imagining him with an afro just to get through those parts. <br /><br />I know characters have ticks, bitting their nails, etc... but, and my creative writing prof has told me this SO MANY TIMES, there's a limit. Please. Please. PLEASEFORTHELOVEOFGOD. Don't go over it.<br /><br />So the story by itself isn't too shabby a piece of work. It pretty much follows the usual romance formula of getting together, evil story element involving past breaking them apart, and then forgiveness, etc... There's a good amount of mystery, and while it's pretty much predictable, it keeps the story flowing. The one thing that did bother me about the plot (and this has to do with the romance as well) is the fact it wasn't a harlequin novel.<br /><br />I know, I usually rant about things that are too harlequin standard plot, but I felt there was a definite lack of a certain event that usual occurs in a harlequin.<br /><br />Yes, people, I'm talking about the sex scene.<br /><br />Maybe I should be a bit more specific. Yes, there was a sex scene in this novel, just like there was a sex scene in Breaking Dawn. Both of them sadly play that fade to black thing, and well..it kinda sucks. Cuz you know sex scenes are kinda fun to read, and also the reason why I read adult romances. :P Ha.<br /><br />No, but seriously having that fade to black thing was a bit of a letdown for me. The whole romance in particular was actually kind of a letdown, not only because it was kind of cheesy and had lots of mushy stuff and more of that OMGSOHOT moments, but because the author kind of paints their relationship sort of saint like. <br /><br />The best example of this is that they pretty much tell each other they love each other before they ever kiss. <br /><br />Seriously? I think I've read more riskay stuff in YA novels. I'm an adult, I'm pretty sure I can handle a little lust. Please don't belittle me by making a romance seem so perfect. Relationships aren't like that, because people aren't like that, so don't take the time to make this a I'VE FOUND MY SOUL MATE, NOW WE CAN LIVE FOREVER AND EVER TWILIGHT STYLE. It isn't real. And I don't like it.<br /><br />The writing, as I've mentioned, is perhaps in addition to the romance one of the worst things about this book. So most of the book is written in 3rd person and changes between characters, which isn't bad. At best it's decent, as they're nothing really special about it, and most of it is riddled with cliches. But it works, and keeps the story going, so I can't really condemn it. While I didn't care for the writing, I have to admit that it wasn't the 3rd person that drove me nuts, but the 1st person infrequent chapters told from the point of view of the hit and runner. <br /><br />*Sigh* This is going to sound very very mean, but the 1st person writing really was some of the worst I'd ever read. I think I wrote better stuff when I was 13 or so. I don't know what it was, I can't pinpoint what I felt was wrong with it, but it was just awkward, and urk. I can't explain it, but as soon as I started to read it, I wanted to run away from the book as fast as I could. Odd, I know, but an utter turn off for me. <br /><br />All in all, A Bend in the Road isn't a bad book. There's a good enough plot, and plenty to entertain. It's not, however, a great, or even possibly a good book. The romance is just lame, the writing is barely decent, and it makes me wonder why and how Sparks makes a living off this stuff. Then, again, A Shore Thing was a NY Bestseller, so go figure. 1.5-2/5</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="620266305225313112">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_67981278">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/67981278" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1014065-shana" class="left imgcol" title="Shana"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1441276222p2/1014065.jpg" alt="Shana" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/67981278?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 19, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1014065-shana" class="user" title="Shana">Shana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/763231.A_Bend_in_the_Road" title="Paperback 9780446611862" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer67981278'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer67981278">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15846021771538545073">I'm a Sparks fan so I wanted to love "A Bend in the Road" from the get-go and although I really enjoyed the first half, the second half felt that much more hollow because of the richness of the first half. IMHO, here are my random thoughts: Brian's character needed to be more fleshed out....I found myself feeling somewhere between loathsome and pity for him and not because we got to know him as a real person, but strictly because of his actions explained from Missy's death forward. As this was t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15846021771538545073">I'm a Sparks fan so I wanted to love "A Bend in the Road" from the get-go and although I really enjoyed the first half, the second half felt that much more hollow because of the richness of the first half. IMHO, here are my random thoughts: Brian's character needed to be more fleshed out....I found myself feeling somewhere between loathsome and pity for him and not because we got to know him as a real person, but strictly because of his actions explained from Missy's death forward. As this was the "big twist" of the book (which I figured out half way through anyhow), I really desired to know more about what drove Brian to react to the accident the way he did. Running off at the scene was completely believable, but stalking the family for a year while hiding in trees, carrying binoculars, watching Miles' son Jonah play at school, and then saying nothing for two years? A bit creepy to me? He obviously needed some serious therapy and there wasn't the slightest nod to this, just fast forward a decade and he's happily married, saving lives in the ER, and just like that he's healthy, healed, and hopeful for the future? A bit hard for me to buy into without more explanation of his journey toward healing, departing from his stalking days, and what the hell was he like before he accidentally killed Missy (saying he was shy and introverted fell short, way short)? So aside from that, I adored Sarah and Jonah and even Sarah's annoying mother. Miles was easy to fall in love with until his rage took over a long three years after his wife's death and meeting the second love of his life - again difficult for me to buy into after seeing his actions begin to reflect a sense of letting go and moving on for himself and his son in the first half of the book. He too obviously needed some serious therapy (obsessing over Missy's supposed "killer" as an almost nightly ritual) and not once did he apologize to Sarah for jumping the gun (no pun intended) accusing her of deceit after all of the tender moments and self-truths they shared. I wanted to smack him upside the head....lol. The brief ending of Sarah seeing Miles return to her, thank God, helped to uplift my waning enthusiasm somewhat in end. But even then, I wanted to see some sort of final dialogue between these two main characters to show that Miles was able to come to the realization that as he lost his wife (Missy), Sarah too, in a way lost someone irrevocably, her brother's innocence coupled with a forever tarnished future for both her brother and herself, knowing that Miles' loss was caused by someone she deeply loved.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_88434439">

        <a href="/review/show/88434439?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 08, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2018505-thomas" class="user" title="Thomas">Thomas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=adult-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">adult-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer88434439">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7746790002447666259">Nicholas Sparks does it again with <em>A Bend in the Road</em>. This book is about a police sheriff named Miles Ryan, who lost his wife Missy in a hit and run car accident three years ago. He has a seven-year-old son named Jonah, who has been suffering nightmares ever since the incident. One afternoon Miles has to go see Jonah's teacher for a parent-teacher conference. Jonah's teacher is the sweet and of course single Sarah Andrews who has recently gone through a heart-breaking divorce. They hit if off a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7746790002447666259">Nicholas Sparks does it again with <em>A Bend in the Road</em>. This book is about a police sheriff named Miles Ryan, who lost his wife Missy in a hit and run car accident three years ago. He has a seven-year-old son named Jonah, who has been suffering nightmares ever since the incident. One afternoon Miles has to go see Jonah's teacher for a parent-teacher conference. Jonah's teacher is the sweet and of course single Sarah Andrews who has recently gone through a heart-breaking divorce. They hit if off and soon they are falling in love.<br /><br />I enjoyed <em>A Bend in the Road</em>. Although it was like a typical romance novel - fluffy, sweet, and has characters that are characterized entirely by their past heartbreak, it was still a good book. Sparks writing style doesn't utilize overly excessive romance terms, and is concise and to the point. The mystery was actually intriguing and the development of Jonah was cute. I just wish it was a little more original.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1425995700">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1425995700" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/47845534-erica-griep" class="left imgcol" title="Erica Griep"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Erica Griep" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1425995700?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 02, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/47845534-erica-griep" class="user" title="Erica Griep">Erica Griep</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/3463.A_Bend_in_the_Road" title="Paperback 9780446696135" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1425995700">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4991584501794275053">A Bend in the Road is a book that comes from a story line of tragedy to the positive things that are the outcome. Miles Ryan seemed to shut down the day is wife was killed in a hit-and-run accident. They have a son Jonah together who has some challenging issues he faces. Miles longs to bring his wife's killer to justice but the case has been open for a while and they have yet to have a suspect. Miles and Jonah live in a small warming community where everyone knows everybody. When Jonah starts se</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4991584501794275053">A Bend in the Road is a book that comes from a story line of tragedy to the positive things that are the outcome. Miles Ryan seemed to shut down the day is wife was killed in a hit-and-run accident. They have a son Jonah together who has some challenging issues he faces. Miles longs to bring his wife's killer to justice but the case has been open for a while and they have yet to have a suspect. Miles and Jonah live in a small warming community where everyone knows everybody. When Jonah starts second grade his new teacher, Sarah, teaches in a way Jonah understands and she helps him in a way that most benefits his abilities. Sarah and Miles become acquaintances and speak small talk here and there when Miles picks Jonah up. Sarah just moved into town where she started to teach. She came from a big city, New York, to where she could have a fresh start in a new place. After her husband cheated and then divorced her it left her devastated, she packed her things and moved to the town to put that horrible time in her past. Her parents live here and she longed to be closer to them for the support and to have someone she could count on. After meeting Jonah’s dad and talking here and there they began realizing their pasts both deal with the loss of a loved one and how they both need a fresh start. They start talking more and more and Jonah brings them closer and they eventually form a relationship with each other. <br /><br />A few things I enjoyed about this book was the fact that the author makes positive outcomes out of a negative past, and how the reader can see that anything can happen. Also, I enjoyed how Miles and Sarah share a common interest in Jonah and how a little boy with so many difficulties can brighten both their days in an instant and brings them closer without even knowing it. Another thing about this book I enjoyed was the overall closeness and warming feel the town brought to the book, they were a support system for both Miles and Sarah and that was special. On the other hand, one thing I didn't like as much was the jealousy Miles first felt from Sarah, which at first drew them apart. The jealously first started with how they both deal with Jonah in different ways and Jonah felt closer with Sarah and always wanted to be with her.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to any reader that likes reading about positive things that come out of tragic pasts, or any reader that is in need of a happy ending with a new family in the outcome. Readers that enjoy some romance and hard love also should read A Bend in the Road.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4991584501794275053">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14870715931539170043">Justiça.<br /><br />O principal factor que move Miles Ryan, é justiça pela morte inexplicada e súbita da mulher Missy. <br /><br />A história começa quando o filho de Miles, Jonah começa a ter problemas de aprendizagem na escola.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText14870715931539170043">Justiça.<br /><br />O principal factor que move Miles Ryan, é justiça pela morte inexplicada e súbita da mulher Missy. <br /><br />A história começa quando o filho de Miles, Jonah começa a ter problemas de aprendizagem na escola. Sarah, a professora oferece-se para umas explicações ao miúdo e a partir daí a relação entre a professora e Miles desenvolve-se. O romance deste casal, achei bonito mas 'mais do mesmo', ou seja típico dos muitos romances de Nicholas Sparks.<br /><br />Mesmo tendo uma relação estável, o acidente da mulher ainda atormenta Miles que procura justiça pelo atropelamento e fuga que roubou a vida a Missy. Inicialmente pensei que o assassino fosse Otis, o vilão que já tinha tido vários problemas com a lei mas depois com o desenrolar da história e com a introdução de outras personagens, pus logo a ideia de parte, pois sabia que a descoberta do condutor seria uma surpresa. Tendo eu já lido vários livros do NS, sabia que essa pessoa seria uma personagem que não teria um papel muito relevante ao longo da acção e acabei por acertar.<br /><br />Foi um livro razoável mas está longe de ser dos melhores do autor, mesmo assim apreciei a leitura.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_740304926">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/740304926" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/23984381-amna-am-240526" class="left imgcol" title="Amna_am_240526"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Amna_am_240526" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/740304926?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 22, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/23984381-amna-am-240526" class="user" title="Amna_am_240526">Amna_am_240526</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/763231.A_Bend_in_the_Road" title="Paperback 9780446611862" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer740304926">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer894977373703886541">A Bend in the Road is a book about a sherif named Miles Ryan who lost hope in almost everything after losing his true love, his wife Missy in a tragic accident. He did not want to live anymore after his loss, however he had his son Jonah to look after. A few years later after Jonah started the second grade, he had a lot of difficulties with his classes so by the request of his teacher Miss Sarah Andrews to meet Miles Ryan everything they both were struggling and living changed.<br />I loved this story</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText894977373703886541">A Bend in the Road is a book about a sherif named Miles Ryan who lost hope in almost everything after losing his true love, his wife Missy in a tragic accident. He did not want to live anymore after his loss, however he had his son Jonah to look after. A few years later after Jonah started the second grade, he had a lot of difficulties with his classes so by the request of his teacher Miss Sarah Andrews to meet Miles Ryan everything they both were struggling and living changed.<br />I loved this story so much because it was written first of all by my favorite author Nicholas Sparks. Second, it is based on a true story that happened to either a family member or a close friend to Nicholas. Third, all his stories are based in North Carolina, which in my opinion shows how much he truly loves his hometown. Finally, the language was really easy to understand, and by the end of every chapter you're very curious to want to know what would happen next. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="894977373703886541">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17547740279113889105">Finally!! This is the kind of book I wanted from Mr. Sparks!! The difference between this and his other books (I read til date) is all books started peacefully and ended with tragedy but here it is vice versa!!<br /><br />The emotional bondage between the lead characters during their different times was narrated so touchingly!! And yeah there is always the sparks kind of romance which is always a worth read!! The death of his wife and the repercussions were narrated in a wonderful way!! The pinch of sentiment, as usual in sparks' books, is a bit on higher note yet it is required for this subject!!<br /><br />This plot is a mixed narration, sometimes first person and sometimes third person!! The relation of the third person with the leads will be revealed slowly once the plot begins to thicken!!<br /><br />On the whole this is a different kind of work , narration wise!! A worth read and definitely a page turner!!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13292713874041230683">Miles Ryans life seemed to end the day his wife was killed in a hit-and-run accident two years ago. As deputy sheriff of New Bern, North Carolina, he not only grieves for her and worries about their young son Jonah but longs to bring the unknown driver to justice. Then Miles meets Sarah Andrews, Jonahs second-grade teacher. A young woman recovering from a difficult divorce, Sarah moved to New Bern hoping to start over.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText13292713874041230683">Miles Ryans life seemed to end the day his wife was killed in a hit-and-run accident two years ago. As deputy sheriff of New Bern, North Carolina, he not only grieves for her and worries about their young son Jonah but longs to bring the unknown driver to justice. Then Miles meets Sarah Andrews, Jonahs second-grade teacher. A young woman recovering from a difficult divorce, Sarah moved to New Bern hoping to start over. Tentatively, Miles and Sarah reach out to each other....and soon they are falling in love. But what neither realizes is that they are also bound together by a shocking secret, one that will force them to reexamine everything they believe inincluding their love. (Amazon.com)</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_955032276">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/955032276" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/27941258-ansley-player" class="left imgcol" title="Ansley Player"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1391711982p2/27941258.jpg" alt="Ansley Player" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/955032276?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 01, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/27941258-ansley-player" class="user" title="Ansley Player">Ansley Player</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/3463.A_Bend_in_the_Road" title="Paperback 9780446696135" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer955032276">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17196050390091041347"> In the book A Bend in the Road, the main character Miles Ryan's wife, Missy Ryan was hit by a car two years ago, leaving Miles alone with their son Jonah. Now after two years of mourning Miles, has come to terms with the fact that, although Missy was the love of his life and someone took that away from him and didn't even confess they just ran away like a coward. Miles, a police officer, knew that he could find his wife's murderer if he just looked at the case enough times and reviewed the evid</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17196050390091041347"> In the book A Bend in the Road, the main character Miles Ryan's wife, Missy Ryan was hit by a car two years ago, leaving Miles alone with their son Jonah. Now after two years of mourning Miles, has come to terms with the fact that, although Missy was the love of his life and someone took that away from him and didn't even confess they just ran away like a coward. Miles, a police officer, knew that he could find his wife's murderer if he just looked at the case enough times and reviewed the evidence enough that he could find the person that killed the best thing that had ever happened to him. Then he meets Sarah Andrews, the new girl in town from Baltimore, and Jonah's new teacher. Sarah Andrews discovers that Jonah is behind all of the other kids his age and needs more help than the normal kids, so she has a conference with Miles and they have an immediate attraction and they agree that Jonah will stay after school three times a week and the other two he will still need help from Miles. As the relationship between Jonah and Sarah grows so does the attraction between Sarah and Miles, and Miles soon starts to come to terms with the fact that Missy died and he should focus on the most important thing in his life right now, Jonah and stops obsessing over the case file of the hit and run. Soon Miles and Sarah become a couple and are practically inseparable, until one day when Sarah's brother admits to being the one who killed Missy and practically stalked Miles and Jonah for a year after her death. Then Miles becomes obsessed again and questions his judgment and his relationship, but soon overcomes this and realizes the Sarah was the best thing that had happened to him since the accident and knows that he and Sarah are meant to be. <br /><br />Overall I enjoyed this book because it had romance and mystery involved in it. I also liked it because it didn't seem as if it were a "stereotypical" Nicholas Sparks book in that I didn't already know what was going to happen at the end before I finished it. But lets face it we all need those "stereotypical" lovey dovey books every once in a while, and although I was expecting that, I didn't receive that at all. Instead I got, romance, suspense, and mystery all in one. I especially liked Sparks shifted the point of view throughout the book from Miles to Sarah to the driver on that night Missy was killed. I also liked it because for once I didn't already know who the killer was, or the criminal, it was a complete surprise that i never even saw coming. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17196050390091041347">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16343515759204752772">I read, "A bend in the Road" by Nicholas Sparks. This a great novel for any person to read, well mostly for people who like a nice romance book to read. This book is not only a romance but it is a great mystery as well. It is about a Sheriff named Miles Ryan who was married to a woman, Missy Ryan, together they had a young son, Jonah. Well one night Missy Ryan was jogging on the side of the road when she was involved in a hit and run accident. She had did that night. For two years Sheriff Miles</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16343515759204752772">I read, "A bend in the Road" by Nicholas Sparks. This a great novel for any person to read, well mostly for people who like a nice romance book to read. This book is not only a romance but it is a great mystery as well. It is about a Sheriff named Miles Ryan who was married to a woman, Missy Ryan, together they had a young son, Jonah. Well one night Missy Ryan was jogging on the side of the road when she was involved in a hit and run accident. She had did that night. For two years Sheriff Miles searched for the person who had killed the love of his life. They never could find out who had ran that night she had died. Well after two years the investigation had begun to slow down and Miles started to live a somewhat of a normal life again, that is until he met Sarah. Sarah was Jonah's school teacher and one night they had a date and sooner or later they had fallen in love. They were both crazy about each other. Although when complications come up again about the person in the car that night that had killed Missy Ryan, things start to bring up complications with Sarah and Miles. Will they find out the person that had killed his wife or not? Will the complications between them clear up or not? </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7176703530594973384">The book A Bend in the Road is definitely 5 stars. A bend in the road is about how this a police officer named Miles lives in a town called New Bern with his son Jonah and also that is where his wife died. Miles as been living there with his son Jonah for a while now and he has been trying to figure out who hit and killed his wife with their car. Once Sarah gets to New Bern she starts teaching at Jonah's school and eventually falls in love with Miles. Then Sarah figures out who killed Miles wife. <span id="freeTextContainer2477010003151142073">A Bend in the Road was a story about loss, love and forgiveness. It was quite a slow moving book especially with the introduction of the main characters Miles and Sarah. Miles lost his wife in a hit-and-run incident and has been bringing up his son Jonah alone. Sarah is Jonahs' school teacher wh0se life becomes intertwined with father and son when she offers to help Jonah catchup on his studies after he falls behind in class. It was a little too perfect how Miles and Sarah's lives matched up con</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2477010003151142073">A Bend in the Road was a story about loss, love and forgiveness. It was quite a slow moving book especially with the introduction of the main characters Miles and Sarah. Miles lost his wife in a hit-and-run incident and has been bringing up his son Jonah alone. Sarah is Jonahs' school teacher wh0se life becomes intertwined with father and son when she offers to help Jonah catchup on his studies after he falls behind in class. It was a little too perfect how Miles and Sarah's lives matched up considering their individual circumstances. Nevertheless it was heartwarming to see them rediscover the joy in loving someone. Underlying the whole romance plot was the persistence of Miles in finding out the person behind his wifes' accident. Turns out to be a shocker which shakes up his world once again and he's faced with a difficult decision.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XA6Gy+xcIhSlRAvTioGcGF6KHFIms8l2K/jWihy43EE52rkYHo427imcf2j04HqqF33fS29ujtxB8dMY0C0qBA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('0M2gaMFnfAysCJOqO97MDe/etwNTCR+DvE9AOW8E5Ry1GZ+7M7Vo9iDQ5xFFvyq/pil0GhrUWCnWRkWro5ETWQ==')})
  }

He graduated in 1984 as valedictorian from Bella Vista High School, then enrolling at the University of Notre Dame, having received a full track and field scholarship. With a mass of wiry braids as uncontrollable as she is, Quinn hides her secret diary in a remote cove and clings fiercely to private mementos of her parents. Support comes to Dana with the unexpected reappearance of an old friend, marine biologist Sam Trevor, whom readers will remember from Firefly Beach. And he\'s been in love with Dana for all the years that have passed between them.Dana cannot begin to contemplate opening her heart again, especially now, especially to a man she can only allow herself to see as a young student. But together, she and Sam begin to discover that Hubbard\'s Point is the center of endless mysteries, and that many of the answers lie in the blue-purple depths that surge through Dana\'s paintings and into all of their lives, revealing the transcendence of love even in the face of grief and death. She is a victim unlike any Julia has ever seen: a child locked in a world of unimaginable fear and isolation. When word spreads of the &amp;quot;wild child&amp;quot; and the infamous doctor who is treating her, the media descend on Julia and once again her competence is challenged. State and federal authorities want to lock the girl away in an institution until an identification can be made. But to Julia, who has come to doubt her own ability, nothing is more important than saving the girl she now calls Alice. To heal this child, Julia will have to understand that she cannot work alone and must look to others--the people in the town she left long ago, the sister she barely knows, and Dr. Max Cerrasin, a handsome, private man with secrets of his own.\n\nThen a shocking revelation forces Julia to risk everything to discover the truth about Alice. The ordeal that follows will test the limits of Julia\'s faith, forgiveness, and love, as she struggles to ascertain where Alice ultimately belongs.\n\nIn her most ambitious novel to date, Kristin     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2345.Nicholas_Sparks">About Nicholas Sparks</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/2345.Nicholas_Sparks"><img alt="2345" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1332884095p2/2345.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer6901872333286041817">As a child, Nicholas Sparks lived in Minnesota, Los Angeles, and Grand Island, Nebraska, finally settling in Fair Oaks, California at the age of eight. His father was a professor, his mother a homemaker, then optometrist's assistant. He lived in Fair Oaks through high school, graduated valedictorian in 1984, and received a full track scholarship to the University of Notre Dame.<br /><br />After breaking the N</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6901872333286041817">As a child, Nicholas Sparks lived in Minnesota, Los Angeles, and Grand Island, Nebraska, finally settling in Fair Oaks, California at the age of eight. His father was a professor, his mother a homemaker, then optometrist's assistant. He lived in Fair Oaks through high school, graduated valedictorian in 1984, and received a full track scholarship to the University of Notre Dame.<br /><br />After breaking the Notre Dame school record as part of a relay team in 1985 as a freshman (a record which still stands), he was injured and spent the summer recovering. During that summer, he wrote his first novel, though it was never published. He majored in Business Finance and graduated with high honors in 1988.<br /><br />He and his wife Catherine, who met on spring break in 1988, were married in July, 1989. While living in Sacramento, he wrote his second novel that same year, though again, it wasn't published. He worked a variety of jobs over the next three years, including real estate appraisal, waiting tables, selling dental products by phone, and started his own small manufacturing business which struggled from the beginning. In 1990, he collaborated on a book with Billy Mills, the Olympic Gold Medalist and it was published by Feather Publishing before later being picked up by Random House. (It was recently re-issued by Hay House Books.) Though it received scant publicity, sales topped 50,000 copies in the first year of release.<br /><br />He began selling pharmaceuticals and moved from Sacramento, California to North Carolina in 1992. In 1994, at the age of 28, he wrote The Notebook over a period of six months. In October, 1995, rights to The Notebook were sold to Warner Books. It was published in October, 1996, and he followed that with Message in a Bottle (1998), A Walk to Remember (1999), The Rescue (2000), A Bend in the Road (2001), and Nights in Rodanthe (2002), The Guardian (2003), The Wedding (2003), Three Weeks with my Brother (2004), True Believer (2005) and At First Sight (2005) all with Warner Books. All were domestic and international best sellers and were translated into more than 35 languages. The movie version of Message in a Bottle was released in 1999, A Walk to Remember was released in 2002, and The Notebook was released in 2004. The average domestic box office gross per film was $56 million -- with another $100 million in DVD sales -- making the novels by Nicholas Sparks one of the most successful franchises in Hollywood.<br /><br />The film rights to Nights in Rodanthe, True Believer and At First Sight have been sold, and Nicholas Sparks has written the screenplay for The Guardian, though he has not offered it for sale at this point.<br /><br />He now has five children: Miles, Ryan, Landon, Lexie, and Savannah. He lives in North Carolina with his wife and children.<br /><br />His ancestry is German, Czech, English, and Irish, he's 5'10" and weighs 180 lbs. He is an avid athlete who runs daily, lifts weights regularly, and competes in Tae Kwon Do. He attends church regularly and reads approximately 125 books a year. He contributes to a variety of local and national charities, and is a major contributor to the Creative Writing Program (MFA) at the University of Notre Dame, where he provides scholarships, internships, and a fellowship annually.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6901872333286041817">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/2345.Nicholas_Sparks" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Nicholas Sparks...</a>
